## REASONSTORESEARCH

Like the vampiresoftheWorldof Darknesshe styles ofmagic in Blood Sacrifice are hased on blend of foilre and fantasy -the legends and fiction of rhesourceculruresas wellastheiractual occult bcliefs.This reinforces rheillusion thr the WorldofDarknesscould bca hiddensidetoourteal world.

More importantly,this gives you moregame material than we could ever publishLibruries and bookstoreshold treasuries oflore everything from collections of follktalesto scholarly anthropoIogical sudiesthat caninspiremore Paths rialscharcters an sries

Remember thongl, that blood magic never preciscly imitates the formsof mortal occult or religious beliefs.Don't feel too bound byrealism (adodgy concept for a game-about vampires）.Filter themyths and legends through the vampirie condition and the rules for Thaumaturgy to make somerhing new thar works within your game.

Nahuallorl tend to mistrust vampires who do not share their mortal ancestry. Students of Wanga generally must devote themselves toane of the Afro-Caribbean teligions. Sadhana mastersreputedly teach their art only to fellow undead brahmins.The FollowersofSetcarelessforancesry than membersof many clons,but many will insist that would-bestudents of theirsorcery also devote themselves to the Dark God.Anoutsidermay have to pass grueling tests ofloyalty and devotion from a prospective mentor... ot else perpetrate an exceedingly dangerous fraud.

Weurge playersand Storytellersto viewtheserestrictions asopportunitiesThe search for magictuition,lore and ingredentscanjustify all sorts of stories.Doesswash bucklingadventure-"IndiannJones ByNight—appcal toyou?Search forthat lost temple or tomb.Do you prefer Creepy,Lovecraftian horror full of hideous secrets and Slimy Unspeakables？What luck.a reclusive vampire avant ina decaying backwoods village s said toknowthe ritualyouseek...and whatanodd staruette he keepson his mantelpiece,lf you enjoy razor-edged intrigue.the chal lenge ofopposed mentors should provide plenty of opportunities.Players can certainly take heir fill of er sonal horror as theircharactersleatmjust how far they will go for the sake of magical power.

## THECHALLENGEFROMBEYOND

The stylesofThaumaturgy described in Blood Sorcery come from regions outside the"developed world that most players and characters know.AsWestern vam piresmcer theircounterparts in (and from}other lands. they encounterunfamiliar bloodmagic aswell.Even in the Westem world,the Tremere now face a minar (but growing)challenge to.their long-assumed monopoly on ThaumarrgyForcenturies in the Camarillaa vampire who sought sorcerou5 aid bad to pay whatever price the

localTremere chargedandsmile.TheTremere ant had the Sabbat over a barrel in much the same way.

Upheavals in both sects and among independent clans have broken thatmonopoly.The destruction of the Tremere antitrbu forces theSabbat toshopforaltermative magical resources.The civil war among the Assamites has launched a dinspora of theirbloodmagicians whopetition both the Sabbat and Camarilla for protection.The Fol lowers of Ser vend their ancient occult prowess for their own obscure reasons.Foreign princes court the blood brahmins just as mortalcorporations recruit computer programmers from India.

In bothfearand fascination,theTremereseck tomaster thesecretartsoftheseotherthaumaturges.Longrestrictedto Europe anditscolonies,ClanTremerenowseeksto expand its base.Globaliration is the new buzzword around the chantries.Everyonecleisdoingit,and theever-competitive Tremere vow not to be leftbehind.

Other Tremere expand their clan beyond its European roots more directly.by Embracing childer from amongtheseforeignpopulations,fromMexicancranderos toIndianholy men.Suchchilderbringan insider'sviewof their culture's magical traditions.The Tremere hope they can adapt native spells and conjurations just as the clan's founders adapted the Hermetic magic ofmedieval Europe. Thus will ClanTremere assemble and synthesize all the magic in the world-or so they hope.

In Africa and India,the Middle East and Central America,Ttemere savants ponder obscure clues within ancient myths andexcavate long-lost temples and tombs. Srudents kneel beforeundead sages,begging tolearn thcir mystic lore.and cunning clders weave vicious schemes to caprure those same sagesand extract secrets through torture.

Some among theTremere doubtthisworld-spanning program.The foreign Thaumaturgy may be too,well, foreign.To learn another culture's magic,Tremere studentsfind they must learn andaccept that culture'sbeliefs. Then,however... are they stillTremereCan the clan's elders trust them?In seeking to encompass all blood sorcery within itself，will Clan Tremere shatter itself beyond hope of reunion?

## BLOODSACRIFICE

When European scholars rediscovered Greek and Roman learningin the laterMiddleAges,theyrecovered theancients'astrology,mysticism andmagic-chieflythe

Many impediments to learning non-Western Thaumaturgy boil down to religion.The Tremere clan culrure isnotveryreligous.SinceancienttimesheWest has denigrated and demonized magic.The Romans,so promiscuously tolerant of foreign religions,frequently launched waves of suppression against astrologers,fortune-tellers and all sorts ofmagicians.The Jewish Law likewisc condemned all sorcery except the mystical Kabbalah. Christianity inherited a suspicion ofmagic frombothsources.St.Augustineof Hippodeclared that an mighty forged an implicit pact with Satan.

Corps Hermeticonalong with Greco-Roman law. medicine,mathandrhetoric.Scholars pursued thisoccult lore at their peril.PioneeringHermetics adopted avariety of dodgesto forestall the inquisitor.Some wrapped their spellsinprayer,and proclaimed thatallmagicworked by the sufferance of God.Others denied themystical aspect of their spells,descrbing them as "natural magicthar cxploited subtleforcesof theplanets,theelemenrsand the human spirit.The founders of Clan Tremere came from this culture.Both as mortals andvampires,they saw their magic as a practical craft with no religious implications.

Apractical,diligentTremeremust make asignificant conceptual leaptoleam theforms of sorcery described in BloodSacrifice.Eachmagical tradition intertwineswith areligious tradition.A student who says,Nevermind the sermon.justteachme howtocastthespelldoesnotlearn much.A bokkor or brahmin believes his magic works because ofhis connectionto thedivine.Hecould nomore divorce his magic from hisfaith than he could divorce the right side of his body from his left.

Not every culrure separatesand opposesmagicandrel gionEgpanpriesHindubranndms combine the roles of priest and magician.Some anthropolo gists say that,A priest has a congregation;a magician has a clientele.Many occult practitioners have boch.

SomeTremere domake that leap.They leamtobelieve inthedivinepowerbehindthebloodsorcery.Notallofthem retum to theirclanto explain what they have leamed.

## GAMEMECHANICS

Tremere paths generally do not require any material ingredient to operate.The vampire might whisper a few magic words to herself or trace a brief gesture to aid her concentration.Some of the non-Hermeticpaths,however, involve a small amulet or othermaterial component to trigger or direct themagic.

All these divergent styles ofThaumaturgy consis of pathsand rituals,just liketheHermeticThaumaturgyofthe TremerndostobyhsamelesllThatugy derivesfrom the supermatural powerwithinvampiric vitac. Schoolsof bloodmagic holddifferentbeliefs about how to evoke and shape that intrinsicmagic,however,and those beliefsexplain their variations inmagical style and content.

HermeticThaumaturgy uses a Willpower roll for all path powersThisreflects the systematic andhomogeneous nature of theTremeresmagicOtherformsofThaumaturgy mayusea different roll foreachpath,generallyanAtribute +Ability roll.

EveryritualcallsforanIntelligence+Occultoll,butthe cultural milieus that underlie styles ofThaumarurgy make differentassumptions about whatOecultmeams.AHemetic magusSanterane andaHindusapossessvery differentbodies ofesotericknowledge andritual practice but theStorytellerSystemfiles them all under the blanket labelofOccultPlayersmaywanttonote thesedifferences on the character'srecord sheet by addinga word to"Oecult":

<!-- image -->

thus"Occult.Egyptian"or"Ocult.Wanga"Charctes who have Occult 4or higher can treat this as a specialry.

AkhuEgpian,Selsotheintemagcalpower possessel by the souls of the dead.The blood magic tradirion ofancient Egypt.now practiced chiefly by the Followersof Set.

Amulet A mogical object that continuously and passtvely protects a person, place or thing.

Ashipu:Babylonian,Magician.A practitioner of Dur-An-Ki.

Dur-An-KiSumerian,"MasterofHleavenandEarth." TheMiddleEastemtraditionof bloodmagic.derivedfrom Mesopotamian,Persian.Jewish.Islamic and many other mortal religiousand magical traditions.

Formula:The instructions for performing a ritual, plus any ingredients or incantations required by those instructions.

Hermetic:Pertaining to the tradition of Westerni ceremonial magic and occultism.

Incantation:Words that a magician speaks,chants or sings as part of magic. Incntations can include prayers. recitationoflegendscommandsnamesofpowerflspirits or uninrelligible words.

Ingredient Amaterialitemrequiredto performaritual. The magic rite might consume the ngredent ike a sacr fce)butamagician can use some ingrediertsmany times (like a magie wand). Sometimes also called a component.

Nahumlli: A practitioner of Nahuallotl.

Leetor Priest:A practitioner of Akhu

NahuallotArare form of blood magic basedupon Azrec,Maya and other native Cental American teligions

Orisha: A Wanga term for the powerful spiritsworshipped in odoun,Santeria and otherAfro-Caribhean religions.Other terms includelou,saint,mystereendok and enkisi.

Path:Acodified sequence of magic powers united bya shared concept.Apathmay focusonaneffect(example:the Lure ofFlames),acomponent (the PathofBlood）.purpose （Hands of Destruction）or any other ideal Path magic usually requires little or no preparation or ingredients.

Rite:The sequenceof actsused to performnon-path bloodmagic.

Relic:An object nssociated (perhaps loosely）with a saint orprophet thar carries a bit of divinepower because of itsconnection ro the holy man.

Ritual Asequence ofactions that produice amagical effect.A ritual requires time to cast,as well assome physicalcomponent and(usually）an incantationtoshape and direct the magic to a desired task.

Sadhu:Sanskrit,"Achiever."A practitioner of Sadhana.

Sadhann:Sanskrit,ArtainingThe Indian tradition of blod magic.chiefly ftom Hindu roots.

SendingThemagic that resus frm aiual,spe cially when directed at a specific peron,place or thing

Subject The reciplent of a magical effect that does not cause direct harm.

Sorcery:Acatchalltermfortraditionsof blood magic other than Tremere Thaumaturgy;thus,Koldunic Sorcery,Setite Sorcery,etc.

Talisman:An object that confers some active,non continuous magical powet ona person,place or thingA talistman may he an Ingredient in a ritual,or nn item of storedmagicthatother people can use

Thaumaturgy: Greek,"Wander WorkingLoosely definedanybloodagiMorspecifallyThmty referstothemagical DisciplineofClanTremere(and most otherblood magiciansintheWesten world),oranyofits paths and tituals.To avoid confusion,Blood Sacrifice usually calls the Tremere arr Hermetic Thaumang

Target:The recipient ofamagical efect,usullyone meant to.cause harm. Also called a victim.

Tradition:A systemor style of magical practiceA thaumaturge'stradition deseribes both the favored proceduresof her magical style and the inner logic that expiains the magic.

Wanga:A bloodmagictraditioninspired byuo andotherAfrican andAfro-Caribbcanreligions andmagi cal beliefs.Also,thistradition's term foraspell or amulet.

True Name:A name that holds thc magicalessence afa person,spirit or thing.

WangateurApractitionerofWanga Somemay call thermselveshoungansbokkor,aymberos rothertile

Working:A less-used variant of sending.especially used for necromantic magic and magic with no clearly defined subject.For instancesurnmoningaspirittoatrack an enemy is a sending summoning a spirit to answer questions isa working.

## THEAFTERLIFE

To theEgyptians,aslong as someone remembered the blessed dead and made offerings at their graves,the dead could retum with blessings for the livingor curses,for mortals whomustreatedthemThe Egyptians buried food furmiture,household goods and measures in their tombs because they expected the dead to use them,m the next world if not in thisone.

The Egyptans believedin rwo realms of the ded The Western Lands,or Amentt,received the souls thar Osiris found worthy.The godAnubis conducted each soul to the judgment-hallofOsiris.There thedeceasedmade thenegative confession,proclaiming his innocenceof 42 stndrd crimes.Anubis weighed the persons heart,orconscience, againstaathrhatmboleaatruhusticn the cowmiccnder.Ifthe personssins weighedmore than the feather,however,amonstercalled theEaterofHeartsstood ready odevour him Ifthedeceased tnily had a sinless heart oriftheproperspellsjiggeredthescalesofjudgment-the godThoth wrote thepersonsname in the Book of Life.The soul then pased to the Westem Lands,The afterlife in Amenti resermbled life on Earth, but magic mnde it more pleasantFor instance,the deceased were obhiged to plowplantand harvest justas they hadonEarth.buta magic spell ould animate hittle statues calledshab into labrer who did the wotk instead

Thesoul'sfree travelbetweenthelandsof the livingand the dead depended,however,on preserving the khat.The cadaver'sdestruction broughr mue death tothe soul,or ar least rendered the ba and ka unable to visit thelivingworld Mummification preerved the body,ensuring the sous immortality,andEgyptianaristocrats built hidden tombs n hopes of protecting their mummies from grave robbers.

Before the Egyptians conceived of Amenti,howevet theybelievedinagrimmerunderworldwhichtheyrerained for the dead who failed the test of OsrisThe Egyptians believed that after it sailedacrossthe sky curing the day,the boat of Ra sailedunder the Eanh through the cavems f Duat,the River of Death.Serpentsmonsters anddemons hanted Duatalthough parts of Duat burned,the nightly passage of Ra gave the only light.The dead consigned to Duat existedwithout food,light,air ormotion.The most ancient spellsandprayerssoughtto deliver the deadperson from this bleak half-existence by adding them to the sunboat's crew,who enjoyed an eternal afterlife with Ra

## MESOPOTAMIANSTATERELIGION

The prlests treared the statesof their godsasf they were living people.The priests"woke"the statue in the marning.dresseditand offereditfoodThe prlests thenate the food offering as the godsleftovers. On special occastonsthey mounted the state inachariot to see and be seenbyitpeople.Supplicantspreented theirrequests tothe statuendbrcghtagift showtheirrespect.The priests didnot own any of the clothesfurnrure other offerings made to rhe god; they merely had use of them as the god's live-inservants.

The temples and inscriptionsaf Mesopotamia come fromstaterelgionsthardealwithfertilty,socialorderand war.The king needed to maintain order so he and his people could properly serye theit gods.Inreturn they prayed for the gods to send them good harvestsabundant progeny for their anials (and themselves）.andvictory aganst rheir rivas.

Godsalso rcccived sacrificialofferingsofanirals,fish or other hings.Sacrificialmethods varicdbut often the priests burned sacrificed animals in a descending trench.

Mesopotamian religton certainly hnd a sexumlele ment.The gods mared just as moral didnd their uionshelped ensre thefertility of thesoilanimal and humans. Statues of god and goddess made conjugal visits. Temple tablets also tell of ceremonialmarringesbe

tween the king ot high priest(standing n fora god）and the god's high priestess.In some cases,the participants mayhaveconsumtedthese sacred marriages.The Greek historian Herodorus claimed that an odd sort ofsacred prostitution took place at the templesofIshtar: kine archcologists doubt hisaccount.Certainly some forms of ceremonialintercouretookplace,buttheMesopotamian records do not discus the matter in detail.

Anashipwhoseekstolearnapathorritualassociated witha parriculargod spends aperiod propitiating thatgod in the properways.Hemakes statueofthe god,offer sacrifices and performs suitable rituals. ## MITHRAANDMITHRAS

Some tine between the 1Oth and 6th centuries BC the prophet Zarathustra,or Zoroaster,radically reshaped the Magian religion.Zoroastrianism demores Mithra toa yaata,one of the second rnk of spiritsafter the aesha spenas(immortalholy ones"）who personify virtues,and AhuraMada("Lord Wisdom),thesupremedeiryof Light and Good.Anga Mayu ot Aman,thespirit of Evil opposed Ahra Mazda fromthe heginning oftimeuntilits destinedend.Zorcastrian warship continues to center on fire,asrhe earthly symbol of Aura Mada's lighr.Holy books called the Zend-Avesta and the Giathas preserve Zoroastrian doctrine.The Muslim conquest of Persia in the7thcenturynearly destroyed Zoroastrianism,butsmall pocketsofthe faithsarviveinlran.Indiahasanother small community of Zoroastrians called the Parseescentered on Bombay.

The mostancient Persianprestscalled magropi tiated numerous gods.Their religion greatly resembled that of their cousins the Aryans who invaded India.They worshippedMithraasagodof the Sunandofoaths and the socil order.Their riuals involved fite and drinking an intoxicatingliquid fernented from the juice ofa plant called hama.

## MAGICTHEORYAND PRACTICE

Sadhanachanged thrugh themillennia.Mostrituals reflect the Brahminist stageofHinduism,whileSadhana paths reflect the ascetic stage.A Hindu blood sorcerer works magic through sacrificesto thegods,meditationand a wide variety of austerities.

The doctrine of maya holds that the ordinary world is an illusion.All material things pass away and become somethingelse.True reality lhes in Brahman,the etemal. transcendent soul of the universe.The essence of Brahman consists of pure,objectless consciousness Becausc the entireuniverse isacollecrive hallucination,anascetic who merges his consciousness with Brahman can.in theory,changetheuniverseany wayhewants.Afterallhe isthe universe.

Hindu beliefsaremmensely complex,diverse and often contradictory.The religion sets only one rest for orthodoxyacceptance of theVedasas the divine basis of all knowledge.The"commentaries""of later theologians. philosophers and magicians travel far indeed from these ancient collections of ritual.myth and lirurgy.Thus. Hindu bloodmagicians do not regard their practices as blasphemousand technically,hey are not.

Karma taps people in the cycle of reincarnation. called samsara.Every deed demandsan cqual and opposite compensation.Theman who beats his wife inone incarnation,for instance,becomes a bartered wife in a later incarmation.Aperson's balance of good or bad deeds determines their status in their next life.A person who accumulates enough merit can win reincanation asa Brahmin,or even a god.A person who accumulares bad krenatssaiahforinernanial demon-perhapsademon inmortalflesh,fated toreceive the Embrace.A person does not need to perform good deedsinordertacumulategood kaathough.Constant thoughrs about a god.sacrifices andasceticpractices also confer merit Indeed,holy men can transfer la from one person to another.

The mysticsdefinethegoaloftheirstudiesasmokha berationfromlusnencarntionand thelimts of mortal existence.Some Hindus scek lihcration through salvation by a god Cthers rcgard moksha as a state of petfect intellectual clarity achieved through logicand philosophy.Still others strive to annihilate an ego they regard as anillusion

Most tndead sadhus seek a simple,straightforward lberation:They want to achieve godike power. The vampiresof India regard themselves as demonsand like all Inan demons,they seekto overthrow he gods and take their place. Indianmyths present their goal as some. thung eminently feasible.

Twoyears later,coalitionoflesser chiefsoverthrew the(weak）kingof thecityofOyo.Vassal territoriesbroke away; wars berween the Yoruba cities continued throughout the following century,Other tribes invaded,snsing opportunity ininstabilityWhilehiswas primarilyawar ofkinethe loealKinred found their domains even further destabilized by the conflict.

Outsiders discoveredWestAfrican blocdmagicin 1794. Louis Doumer Millerand,a well-traveled French Trermere who'dlong been fascinatedby the strangemysticism practiced by Haitian slaves,fled Paris during the Reign ofTerror andused hisperiod of exile to study the roots of those beliefsinWestermAfricaWhile hisprecise activitiesandexperiencesin Beninremainacloselyguarded secret,hediscoursedwithanumberofnarivebloodsorcerersand escaped back to Vienna with his newfound knowledge despite anumber ofnear-fatalattempts tostop him.TheKindred of the Yoruba could now add knowl edge-hungryTremere tothelistofWestermerswhowanted ro exploit them.

In disarrayno longer even marginally unified as people,the Yoruba fell victim to slave traders In ever ircreasing numbers.The Yoruba made up the majority of all slaves shipped from Benin's ports from 1820ro 1840.

Most of theYoruba slaveswere bound for cither Cuba or Brazil,though some of themended up in Haiti and the United States.

The Yoruba still exist today, in Southweit Nigeria. They are,n fact,a more unified people than they have everbeen.Their eligionlourishesthughitsnowjust one among many.Some African Nosferatu still pctice alongside them.as do sotne more inscrutable elements of Kindredsociety.Bythemodennigts,however,uangatears whofollowtheAfro-Caribbeanreligionsfaroutnmber those who still practice the faith in its originnl form （thoughmanyWestem wamgateurs still visit theYoruba intent m leaming the ost ancent histories and secrets of their craft).

## THENEWWORLD

The adaptation of the Yoruba faith into other forms began the instant the first captive tribesman set foct, hungry and frighrened, on the shores of his new and unpleasanr home.Although aspects ofvououn,Santeri andotherscanbe traced back manycenturies,thespecic identifiablerootsof the modemAfro-Caribheanreligions first appeared n the 17th cenrury. Thisdidn't make thebehaviorof the white man right ofcourse, but the morality of a people andthe powerof it spirits were completely separate issnes.

Such an idea is laughable.

## DRACTICALWANGA

Most Tremere maintain that it takes decades,even centuries,to create a workable system ofmagic.Exactly how the slave population af the Americasmanaged to adapt anew system from their oldbeliefsisamysteryeven to the most knowledgeable of thaumaturges.
